Since message_id is unique per message, this caused the system prompt to differ on every turn, busting prefix-based prompt caches on local model providers (llama-server, LM Studio/MLX) and causing full cache rebuilds on every conversation turn.\\n• Why it matters: Cache invalidation on every turn increases latency, costs, and reduces efficiency for local models.\\n• What changed: Moved per-message identifiers from buildInboundMetaSystemPrompt() (system prompt) to buildInboundUserContextPrefix() (user context prefix). System prompt now contains only session-stable routing fields.\\n• What did NOT change (scope boundary): Other metadata fields (sender info, thread starter, forwarded message, chat history) remain unchanged. Separately, smaller models that understand tools semantically but lack native `tool_calls` output silently fail to dispatch tool calls.\\n- Why it matters: Without `num_ctx` passthrough, Ollama defaults to a 2048–4096 token context window, silently truncating conversation history and appearing as complete memory loss. Without tool-call recovery, local models cannot execute tools at all.\\n- What changed:\\n  - `ModelDefinitionSchema` now accepts an optional `options` record for provider-specific passthrough settings.\\n  - `applyConfiguredProviderOverrides` in `model.ts` now propagates `options` so user config reaches the runtime.\\n  - `options.num_ctx` is used as a fallback for `contextWindow` in both the native Ollama stream path and the OpenAI-compat `num_ctx` injection path. The extraction is done once and reused in both places.\\n  - New `recoverToolCallsFromText()` parser in `ollama-stream.ts` extracts structured tool calls from `` XML tags only (fenced JSON code blocks are intentionally excluded per security review). Recovered markup is stripped from text content to prevent history pollution.\\n- What did NOT change (scope boundary): Cloud provider paths, existing `contextWindow` behavior when explicitly set, tool schema generation, the OpenAI-completions/responses tool-call parsing, and fenced JSON code blocks are never interpreted as tool calls.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n- [ ] Feature\\n- [ ] Refactor\\n- [ ] Docs\\n- [ ] Security hardening\\n- [ ] Chore/infra\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Gateway / orchestration\\n- [x] Skills / tool execution\\n- [ ] Auth / tokens\\n- [ ] Memory / storage\\n- [x] Integrations\\n- [x] API / contracts\\n- [ ] UI / DX\\n- [ ] CI/CD / infra\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #50894\\n- Supersedes #51094 (closed — addressed all bot review feedback from that PR)\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n1. Users can now add `\\u0026#34;options\\u0026#34;: {\\u0026#34;num_ctx\\u0026#34;: 8192, ...}` to model definitions in `openclaw.json` without config validation errors.\\n2. The `options` field is properly propagated through model resolution (previously dropped by `applyConfiguredProviderOverrides`).\\n3. When `contextWindow` is not set but `options.num_ctx` is, the value is used as context window size — preventing silent conversation history truncation.\\n4. Without tool-call recovery, local models cannot execute tools at all.\\n- What changed:\\n  - `ModelDefinitionSchema` now accepts an optional `options` record for provider-specific passthrough settings.\\n  - `applyConfiguredProviderOverrides` in `model.ts` now propagates `options` so user config reaches the runtime.\\n  - `options.num_ctx` is used as a fallback for `contextWindow` in both the native Ollama stream path and the OpenAI-compat `num_ctx` injection path. The extraction is done once and reused in both places.\\n  - New `recoverToolCallsFromText()` parser in `ollama-stream.ts` extracts structured tool calls from `` XML tags only (fenced JSON code blocks are intentionally excluded per security review). Recovered markup is stripped from text content to prevent history pollution.\\n- What did NOT change (scope boundary): Cloud provider paths, existing `contextWindow` behavior when explicitly set, tool schema generation, the OpenAI-completions/responses tool-call parsing, and fenced JSON code blocks are never interpreted as tool calls.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n- [ ] Feature\\n- [ ] Refactor\\n- [ ] Docs\\n- [ ] Security hardening\\n- [ ] Chore/infra\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Gateway / orchestration\\n- [x] Skills / tool execution\\n- [ ] Auth / tokens\\n- [ ] Memory / storage\\n- [x] Integrations\\n- [x] API / contracts\\n- [ ] UI / DX\\n- [ ] CI/CD / infra\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #50894\\n- Supersedes #51094 (closed — addressed all bot review feedback from that PR)\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n1. For example, an agent\\nsending an Adaptive Card via the `send` tool in a 1:1 chat could have that card appear in a\\nteam channel instead.\\n\\n### Root cause\\n\\nFor DMs, the inbound context sets `To` as `user:{aadObjectId}`. When the `send` tool later\\nresolves the target via `resolveMSTeamsSendContext`, it calls `findByUserId` in the conversation\\nstore, which iterates all stored conversations and returns the **first** entry matching the\\nuser\\u0026#39;s AAD object ID or Bot Framework ID — with no awareness of conversation type or recency.\\n\\nSince `Object.entries()` iteration order depends on insertion order in the JSON store, the\\nresult is non-deterministic from the user\\u0026#39;s perspective: if the channel/group conversation\\nwas stored before the personal DM, the proactive message is delivered there instead.\\n\\nBoth the filesystem store (`conversation-store-fs.ts`) and the in-memory store\\n(`conversation-store-memory.ts`) share this behavior.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nUpdate `findByUserId` in both store implementations to collect **all** matching entries for a\\nuser, then apply a preference:\\n\\n1. **Prefer `personal` (1:1) conversations** — when a user lookup is performed (typically for\\n   DM-initiated proactive sends), the personal conversation is the semantically correct target.\\n2. **Fall back deterministically** — when no personal conversation exists, the fs store returns\\n   the most recently seen entry (by `lastSeenAt` timestamp, which already exists in the\\n   persisted data), and the memory store returns the first match.\\n\\nThis approach was chosen over changing the `To` format (Option 2 in the issue) or threading\\nsession context (Option 3/4) because:\\n\\n- It fixes the bug at the source (`findByUserId`) without changing the inbound context format,\\n  avoiding downstream breakage in code paths that parse `user:` prefix for DM detection.\\n- It leverages the `conversationType` field already stored in every conversation reference.\\n- It fixes **all** callers of `findByUserId`, not just the DM inbound path.\\n- The `lastSeenAt` field already exists in the fs store data, so no schema changes are needed.\\n\\n## Changed files\\n\\n| File | This caused new threads to see orphaned assistant messages and tool results from unrelated conversations in the same group — but NOT the user messages that triggered them.\\n\\nThe resulting asymmetric context is confusing, breaks isolation, and makes it impossible to start clean conversations via threads.\\n\\nReproduction steps (as documented in #758):\\n1. Observe it contains assistant messages and tool results from the parent session that it should not have\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\n`forkSessionFromParentRuntime()` in `session-fork.runtime.ts` calls `manager.createBranchedSession(leafId)` which copies the parent transcript into the thread\\u0026#39;s JSONL file. The pi-mono branching logic carries assistant messages and tool results but not the user messages that triggered them — producing asymmetric, leaked context in every new thread.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nWrite a clean session file for thread/topic forks instead of branching from the parent transcript. The lobster way. 🦞 \"}},\"created_at\":\"2026-03-24T07:06:31Z\",\"updated_at\":\"2026-03-24T07:08:48Z\"},{\"number\":53458,\"title\":\"fix(msteams): prefer personal conversation in findByUserId to prevent DM misrouting\",\"body\":\"## Problem\\n\\nFixes #51947\\n\\nWhen a user has both a 1:1 DM and a channel/group conversation with the bot, proactive sends\\ninitiated from a DM session may be delivered to the **wrong conversation**. For example, an agent\\nsending an Adaptive Card via the `send` tool in a 1:1 chat could have that card appear in a\\nteam channel instead.\\n\\n### Root cause\\n\\nFor DMs, the inbound context sets `To` as `user:{aadObjectId}`. When the `send` tool later\\nresolves the target via `resolveMSTeamsSendContext`, it calls `findByUserId` in the conversation\\nstore, which iterates all stored conversations and returns the **first** entry matching the\\nuser\\u0026#39;s AAD object ID or Bot Framework ID — with no awareness of conversation type or recency.\\n\\nSince `Object.entries()` iteration order depends on insertion order in the JSON store, the\\nresult is non-deterministic from the user\\u0026#39;s perspective: if the channel/group conversation\\nwas stored before the personal DM, the proactive message is delivered there instead.\\n\\nBoth the filesystem store (`conversation-store-fs.ts`) and the in-memory store\\n(`conversation-store-memory.ts`) share this behavior.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nUpdate `findByUserId` in both store implementations to collect **all** matching entries for a\\nuser, then apply a preference:\\n\\n1. **Prefer `personal` (1:1) conversations** — when a user lookup is performed (typically for\\n   DM-initiated proactive sends), the personal conversation is the semantically correct target.\\n2. **Fall back deterministically** — when no personal conversation exists, the fs store returns\\n   the most recently seen entry (by `lastSeenAt` timestamp, which already exists in the\\n   persisted data), and the memory store returns the first match.\\n\\nThis approach was chosen over changing the `To` format (Option 2 in the issue) or threading\\nsession context (Option 3/4) because:\\n\\n- It fixes the bug at the source (`findByUserId`) without changing the inbound context format,\\n  avoiding downstream breakage in code paths that parse `user:` prefix for DM detection.\\n- It leverages the `conversationType` field already stored in every conversation reference.\\n- It fixes **all** callers of `findByUserId`, not just the DM inbound path.\\n- The `lastSeenAt` field already exists in the fs store data, so no schema changes are needed.\\n\\n## Changed files\\n\\n| File |
